    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer9314900315292359484">It’s been almost a year since October “Toby” Daye averted a war, gave up a county, and suffered personal losses that have left her wishing for a good day’s sleep. She’s tried to focus on her responsibilities—training Quentin, upholding her position as Sylvester’s knight, and paying the bills—but she can’t help feeling like her world is crumbling around her, and her increas</span>
  <span id="freeText9314900315292359484" style="display:none">It’s been almost a year since October “Toby” Daye averted a war, gave up a county, and suffered personal losses that have left her wishing for a good day’s sleep. She’s tried to focus on her responsibilities—training Quentin, upholding her position as Sylvester’s knight, and paying the bills—but she can’t help feeling like her world is crumbling around her, and her increasingly reckless behavior is beginning to worry even her staunchest supporters.<br /><br />To make matters worse, Toby’s just been asked to find another missing child…only this time it’s the changeling daughter of her fellow knight, Etienne, who didn’t even know he was a father until the girl went missing. Her name is Chelsea. She’s a teleporter, like her father. She’s also the kind of changeling the old stories warn about, the ones with all the strength and none of the control. She’s opening doors that were never meant to be opened, releasing dangers that were sealed away centuries before—and there’s a good chance she could destroy Faerie if she isn’t stopped.<br /><br />Now Toby must find Chelsea before time runs out, racing against an unknown deadline and through unknown worlds as she and her allies try to avert disaster. But danger is also stirring in the Court of Cats, and Tybalt may need Toby’s help with the biggest challenge he’s ever faced.<br /><br />Toby thought the last year was bad. She has no idea.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7148361454496048826">Ashes of Honor (October Daye #6), Seanan McGuire<br/><br/>It’s been almost a year since October ‘Toby’ Daye averted a war, gave up a county, and suffered personal losses that have left her wishing for a good day’s sleep. She’s tried to focus on her responsibilities, but she can’t help feeling like her world is crumbling around her – and her increasingly reckless behavior is beginning to worry even her staunchest supporters.<br/><br/>To make matters worse, Toby’s just been asked to find another missing child...only </span>
  <span id="freeText7148361454496048826" style="display:none">Ashes of Honor (October Daye #6), Seanan McGuire<br /><br />It’s been almost a year since October ‘Toby’ Daye averted a war, gave up a county, and suffered personal losses that have left her wishing for a good day’s sleep. She’s tried to focus on her responsibilities, but she can’t help feeling like her world is crumbling around her – and her increasingly reckless behavior is beginning to worry even her staunchest supporters.<br /><br />To make matters worse, Toby’s just been asked to find another missing child...only this time it’s the changeling daughter of her fellow knight, Etienne. <br /><br />Chelsea is the kind of changeling the old stories warn about: the ones with all the strength and none of the control. She’s opening doors that were never meant to be opened, releasing dangers that were sealed away centuries before – and there’s a good chance she could destroy Faerie if she isn’t stopped. <br /><br />Now Toby must find Chelsea before time runs out, racing against an unknown deadline and through unknown worlds as she and her allies try to avert disaster. Toby thought the last year was bad. She has no idea.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز چهاردهم ماه مارس سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: خاکستر افتخار: کتاب ششم از سری اکتبر دای؛ نویسنده: سینان (شانین) مک گوایر (مکگیر)؛<br /><br />یکسال از زمانی که «توبی دای»، از جنگ جلوگیری کرد، میگذرد؛ او از یک ایالت دست کشید، و خسارتها را پذیرفت، او بیشتر کوشش کرده تا بر نقش ویژه ی خود توجه کند، اما نمیتواند بیشتر یاری نماید، احساس میکند دنیایش در حال خرد شدن است؛ رفتار بی پروایش، نگرانی حامیانش را نیز برانگیخته است.؛ <br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 01/05/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_3571593533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3571593533" />
    <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews"><img alt="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492999740p2/66199133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3571593533?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀" href="/user/show/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews">Cece ❀Rants, Raves &amp;Reviews❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=favorite-heroine">favorite-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=fey">fey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=hot-jerks">hot-jerks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=magic-etc">magic-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66199133-cece-rants-raves-reviews?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3571593533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2397257485212574168">This! THIS IS THE REASON I STARTED THIS SERIES <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592161085ra/29646825.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602523575ra/30228314.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>While the other books had hints and glimmers of greatness, this FUCKING ONE brings it all together and has made the whole journey worth it <br/><br/>The <b>worldbuilding</b>?? Fucking brilliant <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Purebloods make knowes, Firstborn make worlds…what did you think my parents made?”<br/>“They made Faerie,” I said.<br/>“They did. And Faerie misses us”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>The action? Just creative tension with building up of important key characters and events combined with that <i> *iconic*</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText2397257485212574168" style="display:none">This! THIS IS THE REASON I STARTED THIS SERIES <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592161085ra/29646825.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602523575ra/30228314.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>While the other books had hints and glimmers of greatness, this FUCKING ONE brings it all together and has made the whole journey worth it <br><br>The <b>worldbuilding</b>?? Fucking brilliant <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Purebloods make knowes, Firstborn make worlds…what did you think my parents made?”<br>“They made Faerie,” I said.<br>“They did. And Faerie misses us”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The action? Just creative tension with building up of important key characters and events combined with that <i> *iconic*</i> McGuire sass <blockquote>
<b><i> “I did not consent to your presence,” she said peevishly. “Please depart, and attempt your political assassination on someone else’s property.”</i></b> </blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491907198ra/22459677.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <b>plot: </b> <br>Find another missing child…. <b>Chelsea</b> who is full of power and potential with no control. To simplifiy it? Its a shitshow <br><br>But our heroine? Heres where it gets a little tricky <br><br>The last couple books, our changeling knight <b>Toby Daye</b> was legit depressed. Her personal losses caused her to lose sight of her values, make reckless decisions, and honestly not behave like the changeling knight we’ve come to know and love <br><blockquote>
<b><i> “You can’t save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn’t fair. Not to you and not to the people who care about you.”</i></b> </blockquote><br>But thanks to her friends and awesome court, in this book Toby has some serious character development and now she the heroine we always knew she could be <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509132826ra/24294244.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602523289ra/30228299.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Toby's official court/squad has been formed and together they solve one major fuck-up after another: <b>Toby, Tybalt, Quinn, Raj, Luidaeg, Ormond, Danny </b><br><br>We’ve had some great characters in this series... but it always felt a little lacking. In this book, now they are all fully developed and interacting with each other which makes for some great group banter <br><blockquote>
<b><i> “What’s going on?”<br>“You nearly died. Again. I put you back together. Again. Oh, and you owe Tybalt and May so many favors I can’t even put it into words”</i></b> </blockquote><br>And now the biggie, <b>Tybalt.</b> Everybody’s favorite ♥Lord of Cats♥ <blockquote>
<b><i>“Tybalt shrugged. “I am sure you would have been fine without me.”<br>“Oh, yeah. I just let you help so you wouldn’t feel useless.”<br>Tybalt spared a small smile. “Quite kind of you.” </i></b> </blockquote><br><br>Okay i have literally been shipping these two fuckers since the first book! Theyve had some serious ups and downs. I mean there was one book Tybalt didnt even make an appearance ^fuck that noise^ <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441620804ra/16130320.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “A smile crossed his face. “If I believed that, I would walk away and never darken your door again. I can forgive you your foolishness only because I know how lost you are. But one day, you’ll have to come back home. When you do, I hope you’ll find me waiting.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br>He is exactly how you expect the Lord of Cats to act. Together they support and <i>*mostly*</i> challenged each other<br><br>I’ve always loved how when they first met, he helps her but in the most dickish way possible i.e. mysterious vague clues. But now *6 goddamn books later* he actively part of Toby’s schemes and reckless decisions <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “How was he supposed to know we’d be total morons and stay together for them to attack us?”<br>“And the logical place for you to go would be here?” asked Tybalt.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581535402ra/28954552.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, I’d read this series just for Tybalt. Overall. I love this series. I love the worldbuilding with the different levels of fey and how it all connects with the Faerie and human world. I love Toby’s character (minus the depressing 4th book) because she always fighting to help others, stand up for herself, and kick Tybalt’s ass as needed hehe <br><br>This the kinda series that gets better and better with each book. So you gotta be in right mood of patience for the buildup and just enjoy each one more and more. But this one? This one truly wowwed me <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “Can’t I? It’s been a long time since I’ve loved someone, but I know what it feels like. When you turn from me, it hurts. When you think badly of me, I think badly of myself. When you do stupid, suicidal things, I want to slap you upside the head and demand to know how you can be so brilliant and so blind at the same time.” Tybalt’s expression was calm. “If that’s not love, what is it?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2225569635808771786">This installment bumped this series up to the top of my urban-paranormal series list! I am so invested in the world building and the characters now, and the looming sense that something bad is around the corner. At the same time the romance is real and awesome, but doesn't overshadow the adventure. October is such a great heroine, she's come a LONG way from the first book in the series, that's for sure! Highly recommend it, can't wait for the next! Of all the "Faerie" urban fantasy series out th</span>
  <span id="freeText2225569635808771786" style="display:none">This installment bumped this series up to the top of my urban-paranormal series list! I am so invested in the world building and the characters now, and the looming sense that something bad is around the corner. At the same time the romance is real and awesome, but doesn't overshadow the adventure. October is such a great heroine, she's come a LONG way from the first book in the series, that's for sure! Highly recommend it, can't wait for the next! Of all the "Faerie" urban fantasy series out there, I enjoy this one the most. If you like the Dark Fever series or Kate Daniels series, you'll def like this one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5930992496584853836">2nd Read: 22/09/15<br/><br/>Still a winner!<br/><br/>First Read: April 25 th (2012)<br/>Can I get a <b>MEOW</b> in Tybalt's honor? :D<br/><br/>WOW, WHAT A STORY!!<br/><br/>Okay, I have to admit that THIS series, is at the moment my favourite urban fantasy series ( in case the fangirling wasn't obvious enough..)<br/>What's there not to like?<br/>We have great characters, great stories, a BEAUTIFUL romance. <b>YES, FINALLY!!!</b><br/> I think that everyone that has been following this series, knows what I'm talking about!   <span id="freeText5930992496584853836" style="display:none">2nd Read: 22/09/15<br /><br />Still a winner!<br /><br />First Read: April 25 th (2012)<br />Can I get a <b>MEOW</b> in Tybalt's honor? :D<br /><br />WOW, WHAT A STORY!!<br /><br />Okay, I have to admit that THIS series, is at the moment my favourite urban fantasy series ( in case the fangirling wasn't obvious enough..)<br />What's there not to like?<br />We have great characters, great stories, a BEAUTIFUL romance. <b>YES, FINALLY!!!</b><br /> I think that everyone that has been following this series, knows what I'm talking about! They're so...perfect for one another. I just feel like drawing tiny hearts all around them!<br /> Their dialogues: I have to say that I loved each and every single one of them.<br /><br />In the other reviews that I've written of the previous books of this series, I've mentioned that every single one of them has a different voice. A very unique voice.<br />The same can be said of this one: This can be considered as the one that changes all...a new road has presented itself on Toby's path. Will she follow it? Or are the memories of a not so distant past too painful, for her to take this chance...<br /><br /> Although Toby begins the book with a more depressive humour due to the events that happened in the last book, one cannot help noticing how distant this one's "mood" is of the first book, that had a very dark setting. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, if this was a fairy tale, it would still be a dark one. <br /><br />But the characters have definitely grown, and one cannot help feeling the strong bonds that have developed amongst this group of friends and mainly the bonds that have developed between our two main characters. Two very stubborn, blind, leading characters....<br /><br />So if you like great stories, with amazing characters, I would suggest you'd give this series a try.<br />I'm so glad I did! :)<br /><br />The only negative point? Is having to wait a year until the next book in the series.....<br />A YEAR. -_-</span>
  <a data-text-id="5930992496584853836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_391333669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391333669" />
    <a title="Ranting Dragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4367400-ranting-dragon"><img alt="Ranting Dragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317746155p2/4367400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391333669?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ranting Dragon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ranting Dragon" href="/user/show/4367400-ranting-dragon">Ranting Dragon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780756407490" href="/book/show/13542786-ashes-of-honor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367400-ranting-dragon?shelf=garrett">garrett</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391333669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17857727836659495243"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.rantingdragon.com/review-of-ashes-of-honor-october-daye-6-by-seanan-mcguire/'>http://www.rantingdragon.com/review-o...</a><br/><br/><br/>The sixth installment of New York Times bestselling author Seanan McGuire’s Toby Daye series, Ashes of Honor, returns us to San Francisco and the world of changeling October Daye.<br/><br/>It’s been a year since the events of the previous novel, One Salt Sea, and Toby still hasn’t fully recovered from the personal losses she sustained during that time. She’s been trying to keep her focus on her responsibilities as Sylvester’s knight and putting in hours training her</span>
  <span id="freeText17857727836659495243" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rantingdragon.com/review-of-ashes-of-honor-october-daye-6-by-seanan-mcguire/">http://www.rantingdragon.com/review-o...</a><br /><br /><br />The sixth installment of New York Times bestselling author Seanan McGuire’s Toby Daye series, Ashes of Honor, returns us to San Francisco and the world of changeling October Daye.<br /><br />It’s been a year since the events of the previous novel, One Salt Sea, and Toby still hasn’t fully recovered from the personal losses she sustained during that time. She’s been trying to keep her focus on her responsibilities as Sylvester’s knight and putting in hours training her squire, Quentin—not to mention trying to pay the bills—but it’s not been working so well. Things have gotten to the point where even her most supportive allies are beginning to worry at her increasingly reckless behaviors.<br /><br />And to top matters off, she’s just been hired to find yet another missing child—except, this time, it’s the changeling daughter of her fellow knight, Etienne. Her name is Chelsea, and, like her father, she is a teleporter, able to open portals between the various realms of Faerie and the mortal plane. She is also the kind of changeling from legend—one with all of the power and none of the control—and is opening doors that have been sealed for centuries, releasing dangers never meant to be seen again. Oh, and there’s the fact that she could destroy the entirety of Faerie if she isn’t found.<br /><br />Toby must find Chelsea before the world ends, facing unknown deadlines and unknown worlds in her attempts to avert complete disaster. And to further complicate matters, things are stirring in the local Court of Cats, and Tybalt needs Toby’s help with the greatest challenge he’s ever faced.<br /><br /><b>The worlds next door</b><br />One of my favorite things about this series is the sheer diversity of the various areas of Faerie that McGuire introduces us to. In each novel, she branches out a bit further, filling in a section here, revealing a bit there. It’s almost like seeing a tree from a distance and then coming closer to focus on an area of leaves and see all of the details. It’s very smooth, the way McGuire incorporates the worldbuilding of the otherworldly realms of Faerie into our own, familiar world. Some have said that urban fantasy isn’t as “good” as epic fantasy because the world is already built. I would direct those of that mindset to McGuire’s work, because not only does she create entirely new worlds, she melds them seamlessly with our world and all of its own history and character.<br /><br /><b>A more straightforward plot than usual</b><br />One of the things I really started noticing about halfway through the novel is that the overall plot of Ashes of Honor isn’t all that complex compared to the last couple of installments in the series. Sure, it has its surprises—this is Seanan McGuire we’re talking about, after all—but all in all, it’s one of the most straightforward of the series. There’s no discovery of multiple plots going on at once, decisions having to be made to save one thing or the other, etc., etc., et al. Rather, the initial problem is just escalated—repeatedly. The more Toby finds out about her case, the more she realizes just how much danger they (and the world) are actually in.<br /><br />However, this straightforward plot isn’t a bad thing. Because of it, Ashes of Honor turns into much more of an internal journey for Toby. Many of the events that occur over the course of the novel force Toby to step back and reevaluate what she knows, how she behaves, and how she feels. As she hunts after Chelsea, so does Toby begin to establish and realize who she is as opposed to who she was. It’s a refreshing change of pace and it feels like the logical next step in Toby’s story, and I believe McGuire executed it exceptionally well.<br /><br /><b>Beautifully crafted characters and relationships</b><br />While Toby’s internal, personal journey is more than enough on its own to make Ashes of Honor stand apart from the rest of the series, the level of character work McGuire throws into the mix makes the book shine. As previously stated, Toby undergoes a deeply personal journey, and has to rediscover who she is. This includes her relationships with everyone around her: May, Etienne, the Ludaieg, and especially Tybalt, to name a few. We garner more insights to the workings of Faerie and the various courts and territories (such as Tamed Lightning) because of these evolving relationships. Some new faces are met, and the amount of life and utter believability McGuire manages to give them in a short time is nothing less than breathtaking. Etienne is quite thoroughly fleshed out as a character, and we get to see how Quentin has matured over the last year. Oh, and Tybalt does some decidedly badass things. Again.<br /><br />And speaking of Tybalt, Ashes of Honor also gives large glimpses into the workings of the Court of Cats, as well into a good chunk of Tybalt’s past. For Toby isn’t the only one going through an internal journey. For both their sakes, Tybalt has to come clean about some rather important things, putting it all out there—something that doesn’t come easily to him. It’s a wondrous thing, to see how these two characters who were once on opposite sides have grown to depend upon each other.<br /><br /><b>Why should you read this book?</b><br />Seanan McGuire has done it again. I always think that the most recent Toby novel will be my favorite, and every time, McGuire ups the ante and puts out a better one. Ashes of Honor finds the balance between being introspective and being action-oriented, and holds that balance exceptionally well. The worldbuilding is natural, flowing, and organic. The characters are real, dynamic, and their relationships are completely believable. With Ashes of Honor, McGuire has crafted a deeply personal and intense story that will keep you on the edge, hoping to be pushed over. In my opinion, it is, hands down, the best Toby to date.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17857727836659495243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16333582709407990643">Yes! Finally! (That's all I'm saying so it can't be a spoiler!)What I like about this series is the development of these characters over time.   <span id="freeText16333582709407990643" style="display:none">Yes! Finally! (That's all I'm saying so it can't be a spoiler!)What I like about this series is the development of these characters over time. Toby may still not look after herself and show a blatant disregard for her own safety, but at least her esteem has risen enough for her to know she has been and is a hero. <div id="review_1574385676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574385676" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1574385676?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574385676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2367778076831642877"><p>13/04/2016 Buddy read with my fellow UF addicts over at BB&B b/c we love this series.</p> <i>“You can’t save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn’t fair. Not to you and not to the people who care about you.”</i> <p>It’s been almost a year since the happening of the last book, and at the beginning of this book it would seem that the fae world has finally managed to break our October Daye. After everything she has lost, she has become reckless, having no care for the risks she takes. And all her fr</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2367778076831642877" style="display:none"><p>13/04/2016 Buddy read with my fellow UF addicts over at BB&amp;B b/c we love this series.</p> <i>“You can’t save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn’t fair. Not to you and not to the people who care about you.”</i> <p>It’s been almost a year since the happening of the last book, and at the beginning of this book it would seem that the fae world has finally managed to break our October Daye. After everything she has lost, she has become reckless, having no care for the risks she takes. And all her friends, and myself included, feared that she was just looking for the fight that would put her out of her misery.</p> <i> “If she opens a door all the way to the Heart of Faerie, it won’t close. <b>The Heart wants people. It’s lonely.</b>And that means it’s going to try to pull her toward it.” </i> <p>Luckily distraction comes from an unexpected source. Etienne, her fellow knight, has just found out that he has a changeling daughter and that she’s missing. But even worse is that she is a teleporter like her father, and very powerful, because she doesn’t have the restrictions that purebloods have. And years ago the fae world was almost destroyed by a powerful teleporter. Because they can open doors that was closed for a reason. </p> <p>This book was a lot more serious than the previous ones. Here we see Toby at a very low point in her life, and honestly, who can blame her. She has lost so much, that it would have been unrealistic if these events didn’t have an effect on her. But as the story progresses, and with help from the people who loves her, she slowly starts to find herself again, and finally realises the dangerous line she has been walking. </p> <blockquote><i><b>Tybalt blinked. Then he snorted a brief laugh, and asked, “October, in the years since your return…has anything not been in some way related to what I told you before? You handed me a hope chest in a dark alley. You took my heart as collateral, and you’ve never returned it.”</b></i></blockquote> <p>FINALLY the romance I have been hoping for happened. Tybalt, the King of Cats, is one of my favorite characters, and here we learn so much more about him. The reason he understands Toby so well, is that he too has experienced heartbreaking loss, and together I think these two will hopefully find the HEA that they both want and deserve. Their banter and interaction is so funny and sweet and romantic. *happy sigh*</p> <p>I love the world-building and plot in this series. Previously we’ve been told about changelings being so much weaker than purebloods, and finally with this instalment we see the other side of the coin. The changelings that are so powerful, that they have trouble controlling their power. And it was fantastic. There was even a fae that had the ability to read luck, and sort of manipulate it. So awesome!</p> <p>I absolutely adore this series. It has everything that a truly wonderful UF series needs: A strong but slightly flawed main character; secondary characters that you are going to love forever; a romance that yes unfortunately has been slow-building, but when it does finally happen it will make your heart so very happy; world-building that will blow your mind; and a plot that continues to be so interesting and ever growing; and beautiful writing. HIGHLY RECOMMENDED. </p> <i>It’s funny how people can change your life without meaning to. Even the fucked-up, crazy people leave everything different when they go away. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2367778076831642877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=book-buddy-recs">book-buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=baa-baa-black-sheep">baa-baa-black-sheep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=because-i-have-to-finish-the-series">because-i-have-to-finish-the-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=family-focused">family-focused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=finished-in-april-2020">finished-in-april-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3296115363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1816389403995502903">I highly doubt anyone will be reading these reviews anymore because I'm becoming somewhat predictable. I'm saying nothing new and living through the same disappointments and clinging to the same small, itty bitty, hopes. It's like a weird Groundhog Day.<br/><br/>Though there are some differences in details, I might as well just say "see previous reviews" but I mean.. there are differences. Like, the ship I was shipping? It has sailed. And I want to be happy but lolz, I'm not? I won't say I wasn't moved a </span>
  <span id="freeText1816389403995502903" style="display:none">I highly doubt anyone will be reading these reviews anymore because I'm becoming somewhat predictable. I'm saying nothing new and living through the same disappointments and clinging to the same small, itty bitty, hopes. It's like a weird Groundhog Day.<br /><br />Though there are some differences in details, I might as well just say "see previous reviews" but I mean.. there are differences. Like, the ship I was shipping? It has sailed. And I want to be happy but lolz, I'm not? I won't say I wasn't moved a bit by some of the confessions and big reveal moments but I'm going to reserve judgment until we get a whole book of them being coupley. There was too much of the maiming, running around, "we'll talk later"s, etc, to revel in the moment. Also for all that I had settled into a slowburn for this.. things kinda went two time speed on busting out a certain phrase. At least on Toby's part.<br /><br />"<i>I've stood by and watched you throw yourself against the walls of the world, because I hoped the impact might shake the sense back into you</i>." &lt;-- this was a nice moment but the quote makes me laugh out of context because the second part of this. what a mood.<br /><br />As for the mystery of the week? Snooze. Toby takes a case, Toby goes up against a strident terrible person being terrible even as Toby tries to help, Toby drinks a lot of coffee (always and forever), Toby talks about wanting coffee, Toby hates her own blood, Toby drinks her own blood, Toby loses lots of blood, Toby lets go of a breath she didn't know she was holding (second time in six books.. not bad overall but my brain, it bleeds).. over and over. It's the worst procedural ever. There is no sense of stake in anything because Toby nearly dies multiple times in each book and the only thing that seems to change is who is being unreasonably rude to her, what new information is revealed that Toby will just go on to ignore, who she's into, and.. well, that's it.<br /><br />That said, I would die for Raj and the Sea Witch. Protect them at all costs. <br /><br />I don't know how McGuire can occasionally write amazing characters like the Sea Witch (so far Raj is just adorable, not complex) and then have so many others that are either one dimensional or inconsistent or both. Some of the shine has even come off the King of Cats for me as I found him way more interesting before his motivations were revealed. It made him more interesting, gave him an edge. I want that back. Additionally, the flip between all the formal talk and then the modern slangs for almost every character who bothers with the formal stuff (I'm not counting the regular modern speakers who dip into formality when the occasion calls for it) drives me nuts. It was particularly bad in this one. Also there were some missed moments on continuity in editing in this one that made me cringe in sympathy because yikes that's never fun.<br /><br />So, yes, for those playing the home game : yet another <i>October Daye</i> read. Yet another two star rating. Yet another "maybe next time.." I'll like/love/enjoy, etc. <br /><br />---<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="&lt;br /&gt;https://atakefromtwocities.home.blog/2020/05/09/ashes-of-honor-by-seanan-mcguire/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Take From Two Cities</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1816389403995502903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8068415162902122847">This is the October Daye book I've been waiting to be written. Things that I have been wanting to see... it's there. In spades. This is book 6 in the October Daye series.<br/><br/>As with the entire series, this is an urban fantasy, not a paranormal romance. The romance is not absent, but it takes a back seat to characters and plot. In my attempt to not spoil anything, all I can say is I am fist pumping in the air like a mofo!<br/><br/>The overall direction of the plot left me a bit worried at first. How many times</span>
  <span id="freeText8068415162902122847" style="display:none">This is the October Daye book I've been waiting to be written. Things that I have been wanting to see... it's there. In spades. This is book 6 in the October Daye series.<br /><br />As with the entire series, this is an urban fantasy, not a paranormal romance. The romance is not absent, but it takes a back seat to characters and plot. In my attempt to not spoil anything, all I can say is I am fist pumping in the air like a mofo!<br /><br />The overall direction of the plot left me a bit worried at first. How many times are there going to be missing kids, and then October has to go looking for them? Sounds more than a wee bit familiar; surprisingly, McGuire was able to still keep this story line unique for the most part.<br /><br />LOVE LOVE LOVE Tybalt, always have, always will. Love that King of Cats! Anyone out there still early in this series, if you LOVE Tybalt like I do, hurry up and get to this book! You'll thank me later!<br /><br />If you haven't tried this series, I recommend it to anyone that likes snarky dialogue, funny movies references, urban fantasy that is not porn... <br /><br />*Re-read 9/5/2013*<br />Still LOVE Tybalt, and getting to <i>listen</i> to the audio book, rather than reading was a new experience. I wasn't totally in love with Tybalt's 'voice' but I didn't hate it either. Toby was awesome, comedic delivery perfect (for those moments), and further solidified my love for this entire series. Absolutely stands up to re-reads! LOVED IT!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2138114919147394859"><b>MY SHIP IS FINALLY SAILING!!!!</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461012438ra/18811648.gif' width='400' height='168' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>OK OK so this series really isn’t about relationships. It is much more UF than PNR and there are mysteries to be solved, plots to be uncovered and a dying Faery to save….BUT MY SHIP IS FINALLY HAPPENING….don’t judge me I’m just really excited about it.<br/><br/>TnT (Toby and Tybalt) finally got some traction. There is kissing, some deep conversations, kissing, admittance of feelings and kissing….did I mention the kissing. *happy dancing on a table* That alone is a great reaso</span>
  <span id="freeText2138114919147394859" style="display:none"><b>MY SHIP IS FINALLY SAILING!!!!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461012438ra/18811648.gif" width="400" height="168" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OK OK so this series really isn’t about relationships. It is much more UF than PNR and there are mysteries to be solved, plots to be uncovered and a dying Faery to save….BUT MY SHIP IS FINALLY HAPPENING….don’t judge me I’m just really excited about it.<br><br>TnT (Toby and Tybalt) finally got some traction. There is kissing, some deep conversations, kissing, admittance of feelings and kissing….did I mention the kissing. *happy dancing on a table* That alone is a great reason to read this book. But more than that are the other plot lines happening, character developments and a changling child to save. After the last book Toby’s friends are a bit worried that perhaps she won’t be able to be unbiased and removed from that kind of situation.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I can do my job.” <br>“Really. You can follow a teenage changeling, stolen from her mortal parent, kept from her fae parent, and feel no personal connection that might cloud your judgment?”</i>
</blockquote><br>Toby is always ready and willing to come to the aide of her friends not matter what the trouble even when it might bring up some of her baggage. As we all know now anytime Toby gets involved there are going to be some interesting times.<br><blockquote>
  <i>”… I retained October to locate her. Unfortunately, there have been complications.” <br><b>“You involved Toby. Of course there have been complications. If you don’t want complications, you buy her a bus ticket and send her to Vancouver to buy those coffee-flavored candy bars they have in Canada.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>They do have a point….but then we the reader would miss out on all the fun.<br><br><b>The Short of It</b><br><br>A teleporting changling teenager has been making portals all over the place and she is really strong. This wouldn’t be a great concern except she is teleporting in to Fae worlds that have been locked and opening then could destabilize the Knowes of this world and end up killing a lot of people. And then said changling disappeared whether she is lost or kidnapped is unknown, however what is known is that she is dangerous.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“If you don’t find her soon, she’s going to start opening doors, and she’s not going to be able to stop. Those doors want to be open, and they’ll force her to keep on going. Killing her won’t undo the damage she has the potential to cause.<b> If she opens a door all the way to the Heart of Faerie, it won’t close. The Heart wants people. It’s lonely.</b> And that means it’s going to try to pull her toward it.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>The other great stuff:</b><br><br>Again I’m loving how this world just keeps opening up and becoming deeper and more vibrant. Not only do we get a look into some of the closed worlds of Faery but also we get more glimpses into The Court of Cats. But I especially liked spending some time with some past favorite characters of mine like April, Quentin, May, The Luidaeg and of course Tybalt.<br><br>But even more I like digging deeper into who and what Toby is and why she seems so desperately to need to help all those around her.<br><blockquote>
  <i><b>“Sometimes I wonder if it’s because you spent so long lost that you must insist on bringing every lost thing home.”</b> Tybalt pushed away from the counter, covering the distance between us in a single fluid motion. He was still wearing his human disguise. I hadn’t noticed it before, not with everything else going on. The smell of pennyroyal radiated from his skin. <b>“You can’t save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn’t fair. Not to you and not to the people who care about you.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Toby has been so broken and lost since coming out of that pond and after the emotional events at the end of the last book it is clear that she has a long road back. But I totally adored all the Tybalt time we get in this book and it became clear why all that sexual tension emanated between them to this great build up. I’m really hoping that this relationship sticks since Tybalt almost always steals the page whenever he is on it.<br><br>I’m desperately looking forward to the next book as each new book opens up just a little more of this fun world and its slightly dark characters.<br></span>

<div id="review_206849915" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206849915" />
    <a title="JB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6252434-jb"><img alt="JB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593031648p2/6252434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206849915?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JB" href="/user/show/6252434-jb">JB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6252434-jb?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206849915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15088345840329327247">Sooooo worth the wait! <br/><br/>The October Day series is, hands-down, one of the best I've read. It offers everything I love - action, a rich, well-imagined world, and a fabulous cast of main & supporting characters. With the exception of A Local Habitation (which I liked, but didn't love), every book has become an instant favorite, and IMO, Ashes of Honor might just be the best yet. <br/><br/>The story picks up about a year after the events of book 5, One Salt Sea. October is still recovering from everything tha</span>
  <span id="freeText15088345840329327247" style="display:none">Sooooo worth the wait! <br /><br />The October Day series is, hands-down, one of the best I've read. It offers everything I love - action, a rich, well-imagined world, and a fabulous cast of main &amp; supporting characters. With the exception of A Local Habitation (which I liked, but didn't love), every book has become an instant favorite, and IMO, Ashes of Honor might just be the best yet. <br /><br />The story picks up about a year after the events of book 5, One Salt Sea. October is still recovering from everything that happened, the personal losses she sustained, and her friends are worried, both about the risks she is willing to take and the wall she's built around herself. She's there, she's functioning, but as Tybalt tells her, she's lost, and everyone is waiting for her to find her way back home. To them, and to herself. <br /><br />The main plot centers around October's quest to find a missing Changeling child. Whose child is a surprise, which I won't give away, but as in any McGuire novel, what seems like a straightforward job is anything but. It's one surprise and near-death moment after the other. Thankfully, October isn't alone. Her friends are with her every step of the way. All of them, it seems - everyone she's met and helped through the last 5 books. May, Quentin, Raj, the Luidaeg, April, Elliot, Walther, Etienne, Jin, Luna, Sylvester, and of course Tybalt....we see them all, some more than others, and yet the story never feels overcrowded. There's a purpose to everyone's presence, a part for all to play. <br /><br />For me, what really drove this novel wasn't finding the missing girl or defeating the bad guys. It was Toby and her various relationships, and seeing her transition from grieving &amp; closing herself off emotionally, because she's afraid of losing someone she cares about (again), to fully embracing the idea that all these people who call themselves her friends &amp; allies are, simply put, her family. They won't leave her. No matter what happens, they'll be there to watch her back, patch up her hurts, and keep her sane &amp; smiling through good days and bad. <br /><br />And then there is Tybalt...ah, Tybalt. Our King of Cats is all over this book, and I couldn't be happier. Love, love, LOVE that man! I can't really say more because too much of it would be spoilery, so I will content myself with this: It's about damn time!!!! <i>*happy dance*</i> <br /><br />Final verdict: Ashes of Honor is f*cking amazing. 5 out of 5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15088345840329327247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1584531760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6233683043059021316">Yay! This is book, folks, where Toby Daye finally wakes up and smells the coffee, both literally and figuratively. Indeed, she is as obsessed with coffee drinking as I am and all the people in her life have learned to make it to her specifications. Plus, she has learned about those people in her life—she cares about them, <i>they care about her</i>, and she should probably get used to that.<br/><br/>It was great to see her accept and even solicit help from her regular crew of friends and to see them all win the </span>
  <span id="freeText6233683043059021316" style="display:none">Yay! This is book, folks, where Toby Daye finally wakes up and smells the coffee, both literally and figuratively. Indeed, she is as obsessed with coffee drinking as I am and all the people in her life have learned to make it to her specifications. Plus, she has learned about those people in her life—she cares about them, <i>they care about her</i>, and she should probably get used to that.<br /><br />It was great to see her accept and even solicit help from her regular crew of friends and to see them all win the day as a team. No more isolation! She &amp; Tybalt are officially great at co-operating to get things done, save each other’s lives, and defend the innocent. Not to mention their excellent chemistry! I also appreciate that this romance element to the story doesn’t over-power the novel. It’s an excellent side dish to a satisfying meal.<br /><br />I think the major reason that I love October is because she is a flawed main character. She has obstacles to overcome, probably as many of them in her own mind as in the real world. And, like all of us, she has to work through her issues until she reaches a place where she can claim a little more happiness. <br /><br />This is the series that started my serious love-affair with all things Fae. It’s a good time to love Fae fantasies, they are everywhere now, but this will always be my first love in that category. Thanks, Seanan McGuire, for hours of happy entertainment.<br /></span>

<div id="review_223338133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223338133" />
    <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life"><img alt="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499618776p2/5112089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223338133?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)" href="/user/show/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life">Lynsey   (A Bookish Life)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5112089-lynsey-a-bookish-life?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223338133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13894583018622163612"><i>
  <b>Toby kicks ass in this high octane addition to the October Daye series.</b>
</i><br/><br/>At this point, six books into the series, we've seen October's character make quite the transformation, both emotionally and physically. From orphaned changeling kid, wandering lost in the human world. To wife and mother, trying to play Fairy Bride. And finally, where we are today; to kickass hero and knight errant to the Duke of Shadowed Hills, friend and ally to the King of Cats and Sea Witch, rescuer of lost kids, acqu</span>
  <span id="freeText13894583018622163612" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Toby kicks ass in this high octane addition to the October Daye series.</b>
</i><br /><br />At this point, six books into the series, we've seen October's character make quite the transformation, both emotionally and physically. From orphaned changeling kid, wandering lost in the human world. To wife and mother, trying to play Fairy Bride. And finally, where we are today; to kickass hero and knight errant to the Duke of Shadowed Hills, friend and ally to the King of Cats and Sea Witch, rescuer of lost kids, acquirer of loyal friends, and just all-round reckless but totally lovable main character with an infectious personality. I absolutely <i>love</i> her! For reals.<br /><br />And throughout all these changes in her circumstances, and the physical changes and power-ups she's gone through that make her now almost as indestructible as May (her former Fetch and kinda twin sister), she's somehow managed to keep that wonderful glibness, that highly inappropriate wit that so often gets her in trouble, but that is hilarious to read.<br /><br />I have to say, Seanan McGuire's writing of Toby's dialogue is <i>so</i> funny, and so...random. I think her humour is quirky and possibly won't be for everyone, but it <i>really</i> tickles me. I often have to stop to do that silent laughing thing when she catches me off guard. I just like the silliness of it, especially when it's completely inappropriately-timed.<br /><br />The plot for ASHES OF HONOR was a little more simplistic than past instalments have been, which I think is a good thing because this world is complex enough without having head-bending, multi-stranded plots to try and wrap my tiny mind around. It's another missing child case; a changeling teleporter this time. Which is problematic since Toby can't exactly follow a teleporter around. But that's why it helps to have friends in high places, such as the Sea Witch who can make a spell for almost any occasion, or the King of Cats who can travel through the shadows (which is almost the same thing as teleporting, but significantly more uncomfortable for a non-Caith Sidh like Toby).<br /><br />There was also a separate subplot surrounding the Court of Cats which brought with it some new and very exiting developments. (You can't see me, but I'm grinning).<br /><br />Most of the characters from past books made and appearance with a few notable exceptions: There was no Queen of the Mists this time (not really sad about that since she's batshit crazy and hates Toby's guts), but also not much mention of Danny the Bridge Troll (who I really like), and no one from the Undersea realm either. But I was happy to see we revisited Tamed Lightning. I love April the techno-Dryad and her complete inability to understand, sarcasm, jokes, emotions or anything said that's not meant 100% literally.<br /><br />The best thing about ASHES OF HONOR for me was seeing the character development of many key players, but especially Toby. It's been a year since the last book (in Toby time as well as our time), and much has changed: Quentin, who's around 18 now, is growing up fast. May is becoming more and more like the twin sister people think she is. The Luidaeg still hasn't killed Toby. And maybe, just maybe, Tybalt doesn't dislike Toby as much as she once liked to believe he did. But at the start of the book, the one person who hasn't changed in the last year or moved on from the sad events of ONE SALT SEA, is Toby. Lucky for her, she's surrounded by awesome peeps who won't let that continue for much longer, and the progress she makes here in this book is immense.<br /><br />For fans of the series, I think this instalment will become a new favourite. It certainly has for me. I feel like McGuire delivered everything I could possibly want from a UF novel, and I simply can't wait for the next one. I still have unanswered questions, but I'm confident McGuire has a master plan set in motion for revealing the answers in due course. For example, when are we going to see Amandine again and where the hell has she been? Who the frack are Quentin's parents? And what did the Sea Witch mean about the Selkies having to pay their debt soon? All these questions and more will have me counting the days until The Chimes at Midnight, which releases September 2013. Go faster time, damn you!<br /><br />Highly recommended.<br />5 Stars ★★★★★ ♥<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13894583018622163612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When you turn from me, it hurts. When you think badly of me, I think badly of myself. The # six, and the series is only getting stronger, which is not the usual norm with the long running UF series. At this point, as my buddy reader Maria says, we have gotten so emotionally invested with the series, that our reviews and ratings have gone way past the objective and deep into the subjective territory. <span id="freeTextContainer11675595602809256076">I'm coming to love the October Daye series. <br/><br/>It is darker than most Urban Fantasy books. It touches on some hard subjects because none of the characters are safe, not even the children. <br/><br/>There are some elements of death, torture, emotional abuse, grieving, bleeding, heartfelt moments and betrayal. <br/><br/>Seanan McGuire has managed to creat an interesting world, heroine and a supporting cast. <br/>Choosing faerie has enabled her to touch madness and the complicated relationship between immortals, who most time</span>
  <span id="freeText11675595602809256076" style="display:none">I'm coming to love the October Daye series. <br /><br />It is darker than most Urban Fantasy books. It touches on some hard subjects because none of the characters are safe, not even the children. <br /><br />There are some elements of death, torture, emotional abuse, grieving, bleeding, heartfelt moments and betrayal. <br /><br />Seanan McGuire has managed to creat an interesting world, heroine and a supporting cast. <br />Choosing faerie has enabled her to touch madness and the complicated relationship between immortals, who most times should live forever. Thus, nothing in the relationships is simple. Each can be infused with pain, longing, betrayal, love and tenderness. <br /><br />Moreover, they do not think like we do. <br /><br />In this book, we finally have something happening, something I wanted to happen from the beginning of Rosemary and Rue.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7619306848345473193">I finished my reread of this book and it still ranks as one of my favorites in the series. But rather than an actual review, which I did for my initial read of the MMP version, I thought I'd just jot down some of my favorite quotes from the book. :-)<br/><br/>"You can't save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn't fair, not to you and not to the people who care about you." ~~ Tybalt/October<br/><br/>Every time I was on the Shadow Roads, Tybalt had me, or Tybalt was coming to get me out of the dark. No m</span>
  <span id="freeText7619306848345473193" style="display:none">I finished my reread of this book and it still ranks as one of my favorites in the series. But rather than an actual review, which I did for my initial read of the MMP version, I thought I'd just jot down some of my favorite quotes from the book. :-)<br /><br />"You can't save everyone and leave yourself lost, October. It isn't fair, not to you and not to the people who care about you." ~~ Tybalt/October<br /><br />Every time I was on the Shadow Roads, Tybalt had me, or Tybalt was coming to get me out of the dark. No matter how cold it was, no matter how dark it was, I always knew someone was going to come and bring me home. There's power in that. ~~ October<br /><br />I left my fingers balanced on the floor, letting his blood sing its song of pain and longing. Longing to live, refusal to let go of the world. Maybe that's what differentiates the Kings and Queens of Cats from the rest of Faerie. They have a cat's stubbornness and the power to back it up. So when Death says, "Go", they just refuse. ~~ October/Tybalt<br /><br />Finally, he said, "Some of us, October, will not leave you." ~~ Tybalt<br /><br />"Yes, I have a car. I don't drive much, but how did you think I got out to Half Moon Bay before I met you? I sure as shit didn't fly. I don't have the figure for it." ~~ Luidaeg<br /><br />Kissing Tybalt was like standing too close to an open fire, all heat and the promise of pain if I came any closer. ~~ October<br /><br />"I've stood by and watched you throw yourself against the walls of the world, because I hoped the impact might shake the sense back into you. We do not raise the dead by mourning them so fiercely that we join them. I wish we could. It doesn't work that way." ~~ Tybalt/October<br /><br />She'd already died for me once. If she thought I was mad at her for not dying for me a second time, I was doing something unforgivably wrong. ~~ October/May<br /><br />“It’s been a long time since I’ve loved someone, but I know what it feels like. When you turn from me, it hurts. When you think badly of me, I think badly of myself. When you do stupid, suicidal things, I want to slap you upside the head and demand to know how you can be so brilliant and so blind at the same time.” Tybalt’s expression was calm. “If that’s not love, what is it?” ~~ Tybalt/October<br /><br /><br />Tybalt blinked. Then he snorted a brief laugh, and asked, "October, in the years since your return...has anything <i>not</i> been in some way related to what I told you before? You handed me a hope chest in a dark alley. You took my heart as collateral, and you've never returned it." ~~ Tybalt/October<br /><br />Nothing stays the same for long, not in Faerie, not in the human world, not anywhere, but some things are worth starting, just like some things are worth fighting for. ~~ October<br /><br />Maybe that was all Tybalt and I would have - a chance - but as he put his hands around my waist and pulled me closer, I found I didn't care. Sometimes a chance is more than enough. Sometimes that's all you need to have everything. ~~ October</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1672309461" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387526203p2/4731410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672309461?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=kidnapping-hostage">kidnapping-hostage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=feline-shifters">feline-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=private-investigator-security">private-investigator-security</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=celtic-mythology">celtic-mythology</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672309461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6280697952957182914"><b>Ashes of Honor</b><br/>4 Stars<br/><br/>Still recovering from the aftermath of her last case, Changeling PI, Toby Daye, is struggling to live up to her responsibilities. The last thing she wants or needs is a new investigation. But things never did run smoothly for Toby, so when a fellow knight approaches her with a request to find his missing daughter, she soon finds herself in pursuit of a young girl with the power to destroy all of Faerie if she isn't stopped. <br/><br/>Definitely the best installment in the series both </span>
  <span id="freeText6280697952957182914" style="display:none"><b>Ashes of Honor</b><br />4 Stars<br /><br />Still recovering from the aftermath of her last case, Changeling PI, Toby Daye, is struggling to live up to her responsibilities. The last thing she wants or needs is a new investigation. But things never did run smoothly for Toby, so when a fellow knight approaches her with a request to find his missing daughter, she soon finds herself in pursuit of a young girl with the power to destroy all of Faerie if she isn't stopped. <br /><br />Definitely the best installment in the series both in terms of plot and character development. <br /><br />The plot is comprised of several seemingly separate storylines that all eventually come together to form a cohesive whole. While some are predictable, others are surprising and result in some compelling twists. The action scenes are exciting and there are one or two very dicey moments for Toby and her allies. <br /><br />In terms of the world building, readers are introduced to several knew locations in the fae universe and the descriptions are, once again, rich in detail and symbolism. <br /><br />Of course, the true highlight of the story is Toby's interactions with her makeshift family. Now that Connor is out of the picture, Toby finally comes to her senses and realizes that Tybalt has always been "The One". Raj and Quentin, May and Jaz, and even the Luidaeg all put in an appearance and demonstrate just how far Toby has come in accepting that she is loved. <br /><br />All in all, this series is fulfilling its potential and it looks the Pure Bloods' despicable attitude toward the Changelings will be coming to a head in the next book. Looking forward to it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6280697952957182914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2090519897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Bunnycore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50919516-bunnycore"><img alt="Bunnycore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546238957p2/50919516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2090519897?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bunnycore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bunnycore" href="/user/show/50919516-bunnycore">Bunnycore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780756407490" href="/book/show/13542786-ashes-of-honor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50919516-bunnycore?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50919516-bunnycore?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50919516-bunnycore?shelf=massmarket-paperback">massmarket-paperback</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090519897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1238238358807179526">There are so many things I can say about this book. <br/><br/>Hands down one of my favorites so far, Toby is back. She is trying to heal from the pain of losing Connor. When Etiane shows up and asks her to find his daughter. <br/><br/>A portal jumper that is causing she and havoc in the Faerie realm hasn't been given a choice. <br/><br/>I feel this book was a turning point for many of our friends. Most of them good, I said it before and I will say it again. I love the family October is building. She has amazing people in her</span>
  <span id="freeText1238238358807179526" style="display:none">There are so many things I can say about this book. <br /><br />Hands down one of my favorites so far, Toby is back. She is trying to heal from the pain of losing Connor. When Etiane shows up and asks her to find his daughter. <br /><br />A portal jumper that is causing she and havoc in the Faerie realm hasn't been given a choice. <br /><br />I feel this book was a turning point for many of our friends. Most of them good, I said it before and I will say it again. I love the family October is building. She has amazing people in her life and I fall a little more in love with them all. <br /><br />Is just me or does anyone else get a little thrill when Tybalt calls her ' little fish'? <br /><br />I can't be the only one, and that has to be my favorite term of endearment any man or a cat can use on a woman. I make no secrets when I say he is my favorite character. I like many other women out there have a lot of book lusts but Tybalt is by far my top five. <br /><br />This book made me cry, it made me laugh a lot and it made me swoon and smile. I can't wait to see what happens next and lucky for me I don't have to. I need to see what happens to Toby and the gang, these books just get better and better. <br /><br />I hope y'all enjoy and happy reading!!</span>
